For kernel 1, each block handles (b, i, j), computing all d outputs. ```cuda __global__ void compute_fused_kernel( const float* nodes, const float* pair_feats, const float* edge_mask, const float* w1_T, const float* b1, const float* w2_T, const float* b2, float* fused, int B, int N, int D, int P, int H) { int b = blockIdx.x; int i = blockIdx.y; int j = blockIdx.z; int tid = threadIdx.x; __shared__ float s_z1[192]; __shared__ float s_node_i[96]; __shared__ float s_node_j[96]; __shared__ float s_pair[16]; // Collaborative load of inputs for (int idx = tid; idx < D; idx += blockDim.x) { s_node_i[idx] = nodes[(b * N + i) * D + idx]; } for (int idx = tid; idx < D; idx += blockDim.x) { s_node_j[idx] = nodes[(b * N + j) * D + idx]; } for (int idx = tid; idx < P; idx += blockDim.x) { s_pair[idx] = pair_feats[((b * N + i) * N + j) * P + idx]; } __syncthreads(); float mask_val = edge_mask[((b * N + i) * N + j)]; // Compute z1 collaboratively for (int h = tid; h < H; h += blockDim.x) { float acc = b1[h]; for (int k = 0; k < D; ++k) { acc += w1_T[k * H + h] * s_node_i[k]; } for (int k = 0; k < D; ++k) { acc += w1_T[(D + k) * H + h] * s_node_j[k]; } for (int k = 0; k < P; ++k) { acc += w1_T[(2 * D + k) * H + h] * s_pair[k]; } float sig = 1.0f / (1.0f + expf(-acc)); s_z1[h] = acc * sig; } __syncthreads(); // Compute z2 for each d for (int d = tid; d < D; d += blockDim.x) { float val = b2[d]; for (int h = 0; h < H; ++h) { val += w2_T[h * D + d] * s_z1[h]; } if (mask_val <= 0.5f) { val = -FLT_MAX; } fused[((b * N + i) * N + j) * D + d] = val; } } ``` For kernel 2: ```cuda __global__ void reduce_ln_kernel( const float* fused, const float* edge_mask, const float* nodes, const float* ln_w, const float* ln_b, float* out, int B, int N, int D, int H) // H not needed { int b = blockIdx.x; int i = blockIdx.y; int tid = threadIdx.x; __shared__ float s_max[96]; __shared__ float s_node_i[96]; __shared__ float s_red[128]; for (int idx = tid; idx < D; idx += blockDim.x) { s_node_i[idx] = nodes[(b * N + i) * D + idx]; s_max[idx] = -FLT_MAX; } __syncthreads(); // Max over j for (int d = tid; d < D; d += blockDim.x) { float max_val = -FLT_MAX; for (int j = 0; j < N; ++j) { float val = fused[((b * N + i) * N + j) * D + d]; if (val > max_val) { max_val = val; } } s_max[d] = max_val; } __syncthreads(); // LayerNorm float local_sum = 0.0f; for (int idx = tid; idx < D; idx += blockDim.x) { local_sum += s_max[idx]; } s_red[tid] = local_sum; __syncthreads(); #pragma unroll for (int stride = blockDim.x / 2; stride > 0; stride >>= 1) { if (tid < stride) { s_red[tid] += s_red[tid + stride]; } __syncthreads(); } float mean = s_red[0] / D; float local_var = 0.0f; for (int idx = tid; idx < D; idx += blockDim.x) { float diff = s_max[idx] - mean; local_var += diff * diff; } s_red[tid] = local_var; __syncthreads(); #pragma unroll for (int stride = blockDim.x / 2; stride > 0; stride >>= 1) { if (tid < stride) { s_red[tid] += s_red[tid + stride]; } __syncthreads(); } float var = s_red[0] / D; float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + 1e-5f); for (int idx = tid; idx < D; idx += blockDim.x) { float v = s_max[idx]; float norm = (v - mean) * inv_std; float o = norm * ln_w[idx] + ln_b[idx]; o += s_node_i[idx]; out[(b * N + i) * D + idx] = o; } } ``` Wait, there's an issue with kernel 2. The reduction shared memory `s_red` needs to be sized for `blockDim.x`. If blockDim.x = 128, s_red needs 128 elements. But I used `#pragma unroll` with `blockDim.x / 2` which requires dynamic unrolling... actually, `#pragma unroll` only works with compile-time constants. Since `blockDim.x` is dynamic, the compiler can't fully unroll. For the reduction, I might need to use a constant block size and size s_red accordingly. Or just not unroll and let the compiler handle it. Since the reduction is only log2(128) = 7 steps, unrolling isn't critical. Let me just use a fixed block size for kernel 2. For w2_T, the access pattern is `w2_T[h * D + d]` with d varying by thread. This means all threads in a warp read consecutive floats in memory (coalesced). This is already the optimal global memory access pattern. So pre-loading w2_T to shared memory wouldn't help much for coalescing, but it might save L2 bandwidth if we can keep it resident. But since it doesn't fit in shared memory alongside w1_T, I'll leave it in global/L2. Actually, I just thought of something. What if I DON'T pre-load w1_T to shared memory, but instead pre-load the data (nodes_j, pairs) and keep weights in L2? The weight access is coalesced and L2 bandwidth is high. Let me compare: - With w1_T in shared memory: 24 iterations of h-loop read from shared memory (very fast, ~20+ TB/s effective bandwidth). - Without w1_T in shared memory: 24 iterations read from L2 (maybe ~10 TB/s effective). The difference might be 2x for the h-loop. Let's see what proportion of time is in the h-loop. Total ops per j: ~58K h-loop: ~40K (69%) d-loop: ~18K (31%) So if h-loop is 2x faster with shared memory, total per j improves by ~35%. This is significant! And the cost to load w1_T to shared memory is small (160KB, one-time). So it's worth it. Let me include w1_T in shared memory. Here's the complete code:

+ H; // [D]\n float* s_red = s_max + D; // [BLOCK_SIZE]\n\n // Load w1_T into shared memory\n for (int idx = tid; idx < L * H; idx += BLOCK_SIZE) {\n s_w1[idx] = w1_T[idx];\n }\n\n // Load node_i\n reasoning
The compile passed. Let me check correctness, then also test performance. But first let me think about shared memory bounds. For the given problem: - B=4, N=24, dim=96, pair_dim=16, hidden=192 Shared memory needed: - L*H = (2*96 + 16)*192 = 208*192 = 39936 - D = 96 - N*D = 24*96 = 2304 - N*P = 24*16 = 384 - H = 192 - D = 96 - BLOCK_SIZE = 192 Total = 39936 + 96 + 2304 + 384 + 192 + 96 + 192 = 43200 bytes = 42.2 KB That fits within 227 KB. But I'm replicating node_j and pair data for each block. Since we have B*N = 96 blocks, each with N*D + N*P = 2688 floats of input data = 10.5 KB. So while one block uses 42.2 KB, 96 blocks total would require a lot more if resident simultaneously, but that's fine since they won't all be. However, the issue is that this approach loads all nodes_j and pair data for a single (b, i) at once. It then processes all j. This could be faster because: 1. w1_T is in shared memory (coalesced loads) 2. All node_j and pair data for this (b, i) is loaded once from DRAM But it also uses more shared memory, possibly limiting occupancy. Let me check correctness first, and then maybe optimize further by also caching w2_T in shared memory. Actually, w2_T is H*D = 192*96 = 18432 bytes. Adding that would be useful too and still fit within 227 KB. Actually, let me first see if this version even runs correctly. If so, I'll also try caching w2_T and see if that's better.

More blocks per SM = higher occupancy. - Also, I should try to use vectorized loads (float4) for weights and activations to improve bandwidth usage. - Another approach: each thread handles a single output dimension completely (for all j), and we keep the weights in registers. Then for each j, the thread reads node_i[D], node_j[D], pair_ij[P], computes the first linear (reading w1 of size L*H, each thread needs H floats), then computes the shared-reduced H dimension for second linear. - Wait, if BLOCK_SIZE=96 and each thread handles one d, then in the second linear each thread only reads w2_T[..., d] (H floats) and s_z1[...] (H floats shared). This is very bandwidth-light on weights since each thread reads H floats per j = 192 floats/j = 768 bytes/j, and there are 24 j's, so ~18KB total weight reads per thread per (b,i). Plus 24*L = ~5KB for nodes/pairs. Total ~23KB. Since a warp has 32 threads and reads w2_T simultaneously, maybe coalescing is good? Wait, no - w2_T is transposed, so w2_T[..., d_offset + 0] to w2_T[..., d_offset + 31] are contiguous, so a warp reading the same h but contiguous d should be coalesced. But since each thread needs all H, it would be strided across H for a single d. So threads in a warp read at the same offset, that's broadcast, not coalesced - but still cached. In L2, the w2_T row for each h is repeated: w2_T[h*D + d] for different d but same h. Actually for a fixed h, all threads read w2_T[h*D + d], which is strided by D. So broadcast-like reads, which isn't great for HBM. Actually, forget preloading everything. Let me just go back to v1 and optimize: 1. Use BLOCK_SIZE=128 (or 96) instead of 256 to improve occupancy. 2. Pre-load node_i into shared memory but not other nodes. Do the inner j loop. 3. Make sure to avoid __syncthreads between Phase 1 and Phase 2 since different parts of block work on different arrays (s_z1 and s_max). Actually the second phase reads s_z1 written by first phase, so we need __syncthreads. 4. Maybe load pair_feats and nodes_j using float4 to save instructions. Wait, maybe the better approach is: - Threads in a warp cooperate on one j, computing the first linear. Then they work on the second linear together. - A warp has 32 threads. For first linear output H=192, we'd need 6 warps. - For second linear output D=96, we'd need 3 warps. - BLOCK_SIZE = 192 = 6 warps. Each block handles one j at a time with cooperative computing. Actually, let me rethink with a cooperative-block approach: For each j iteration: - Threads 0..L-1 (or wrap partition) load x into shared. - Then compute w1 * x: - Each thread h computes one hidden unit? Actually 192 threads would work: thread h computes dot(w1[:, h], x). That's 192 threads = H. But we also need more for the second linear. - We have 192 threads. They compute z1[h] for h in [0, H). Then __syncthreads(). - Then they compute z2[d] for d in [0, D). Only 96 of 192 threads are active for this. Thread d computes dot(w2[:, d], z1). - The block does one j at a time. After computing z2[d], update s_max[d] for this j. - This would require BLOCK_SIZE = max(H, D) = 192. But our BLOCK_SIZE was already 256 > 192. We could set exactly 192. Wait, but then how many blocks per SM? 192 threads * shared memory. If shared memory is small (just L + H + D + 192 ≈ 700 floats = 2.8KB), then 228KB / 2.8KB ≈ 81 blocks per SM, but limited to 32 blocks. So occupancy is 32 * 192 / (max threads per SM = 2048) = 3072/2048 = 1.5? Wait, 32 * 192 = 6144 threads per SM? But H100 has 2048 threads per SM (on Hopper). Actually, H100 has 2048 threads per SM. So max 10 blocks of 192 threads per SM. Still good. Let me try using BLOCK_SIZE=192 and see if that helps. Actually, let me first try to just run v1 and check why it was correct but might be slow. The correctness passed. Now I need to optimize speed. For speed, the bottlenecks in v1 are: 1. Memory bandwidth: reading pair_feats N times per i, reading nodes_j N times, reading w1_T and w2_T repeatedly. 2. Since we use 256 threads and the work is small, we have low occupancy but memory bandwidth might still be the limit. Let me try preloading some stuff into shared memory in a smarter way. I'll use registers aggressively for node_i and avoid repeated reads. Actually, I found the problem with v2: shared memory size was 168KB but default max dynamic shared memory is 48KB (or 96KB on some arch) without explicit function attribute. I need to set `cudaFuncSetAttribute` in the host wrapper. Let me try this. If I can get v2 working, it might be faster because it preloads w1_T and all nodes/pairs, removing redundant HBM reads. Let me add `cudaFuncSetAttribute` in the torch wrapper.

0; stride >>= 1) {\n if (tid < stride) {\n s_red[tid] += s_red[tid + stride];\n }\n __syncthreads();\n }\n float mean = s_red[0] / D;\n\n // Variance\n float local_var = 0.0f;\n for (int idx = tid; stride > 0; stride >>= 1) {\n if (tid < stride) {\n s_red[tid] += s_red[tid + stride];\n }\n __syncthreads();\n }\n float var = s_red[0] / D;\n float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + 1e-5f);\n\n // Final residual output\n for (int idx = tid; idx < D; idx += BLOCK_SIZE) {\n float v = s_max[idx];\n float norm = (v - mean) * inv_std;\n float o = norm * ln_w[idx] + ln_b[idx];\n o += s_x[idx]; // residual node_i\n out[(b * N + i) * D + idx] = o;\n }\n}\n\ntorch::Tensor fused_scene_graph_forward(\n torch::Tensor nodes,\n torch::Tensor pair_feats,\n torch::Tensor edge_mask,\n torch::Tensor w1_T,\n import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline

cpp_source = """
torch::Tensor fused_scene_graph_forward(
    torch::Tensor nodes,
    torch::Tensor pair_feats,
    torch::Tensor edge_mask,
    torch::Tensor w1_T,
    torch::Tensor b1,
    torch::Tensor w2_T,
    torch::Tensor b2,
    torch::Tensor ln_w,
    torch::Tensor ln_b);
"""

cuda_source = r"""
#include <torch/extension.h>
#include <cuda.h>
#include <cuda_runtime.h>
#include <float.h>
#include <math.h>

#define BLOCK_SIZE 256

__global__ void fused_scene_graph_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ nodes,
    const float* __restrict__ pair_feats,
    const float* __restrict__ edge_mask,
    const float* __restrict__ w1_T,
    const float* __restrict__ b1,
    const float* __restrict__ w2_T,
    const float* __restrict__ b2,
    const float* __restrict__ ln_w,
    const float* __restrict__ ln_b,
    float* __restrict__ out,
    int B, int N, int D, int P, int H)
{
    const int tid = threadIdx.x;
    const int b = blockIdx.x;
    const int i = blockIdx.y;
    const int L = 2 * D + P;

    extern __shared__ float s_mem[];
    float* s_x = s_mem;            // [L]
    float* s_z1 = s_x + L;         // [H]
    float* s_max = s_z1 + H;       // [D]
    float* s_red = s_max + D;      // [BLOCK_SIZE]

    // Load node_i into first D slots of s_x
    const float* node_i_ptr = nodes + (b * N + i) * D;
    for (int idx = tid; idx < D; idx += BLOCK_SIZE) {
        s_x[idx] = node_i_ptr[idx];
    }
    __syncthreads();

    // Initialize running max to -FLT_MAX
    for (int idx = tid; idx < D; idx += BLOCK_SIZE) {
        s_max[idx] = -FLT_MAX;
    }
    __syncthreads();

    for (int j = 0; j < N; ++j) {
        // Load node_j and pair_feats into shared memory
        const float* node_j_ptr = nodes + (b * N + j) * D;
        const float* pair_ptr = pair_feats + ((b * N + i) * N + j) * P;

        for (int idx = tid; idx < D; idx += BLOCK_SIZE) {
            s_x[D + idx] = node_j_ptr[idx];
        }
        for (int idx = tid; idx < P; idx += BLOCK_SIZE) {
            s_x[2 * D + idx] = pair_ptr[idx];
        }
        __syncthreads();

        float mask_val = edge_mask[((b * N + i) * N + j)];

        // Phase 1: first linear + SiLU
        for (int h = tid; h < H; h += BLOCK_SIZE) {
            float acc = b1[h];
            #pragma unroll 8
            for (int k = 0; k < L; ++k) {
                acc += w1_T[k * H + h] * s_x[k];
            }
            float sig = 1.0f / (1.0f + expf(-acc));
            s_z1[h] = acc * sig;
        }
        __syncthreads();

        // Phase 2: second linear, mask, and running max
        for (int d = tid; d < D; d += BLOCK_SIZE) {
            float val = b2[d];
            #pragma unroll 4
            for (int h = 0; h < H; ++h) {
                val += w2_T[h * D + d] * s_z1[h];
            }
            if (mask_val <= 0.5f) {
                val = -FLT_MAX;
            }
            if (val > s_max[d]) {
                s_max[d] = val;
            }
        }
        __syncthreads();
    }

    // LayerNorm: compute mean
    float local_sum = 0.0f;
    for (int idx = tid; idx < D; idx += BLOCK_SIZE) {
        local_sum += s_max[idx];
    }
    s_red[tid] = local_sum;
    __syncthreads();

    #pragma unroll
    for (int stride = BLOCK_SIZE / 2; stride > 0; stride >>= 1) {
        if (tid < stride) {
            s_red[tid] += s_red[tid + stride];
        }
        __syncthreads();
    }
    float mean = s_red[0] / D;

    // Variance
    float local_var = 0.0f;
    for (int idx = tid; idx < D; idx += BLOCK_SIZE) {
        float diff = s_max[idx] - mean;
        local_var += diff * diff;
    }
    s_red[tid] = local_var;
    __syncthreads();

    #pragma unroll
    for (int stride = BLOCK_SIZE / 2; stride > 0; stride >>= 1) {
        if (tid < stride) {
            s_red[tid] += s_red[tid + stride];
        }
        __syncthreads();
    }
    float var = s_red[0] / D;
    float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + 1e-5f);

    // Final residual output
    for (int idx = tid; idx < D; idx += BLOCK_SIZE) {
        float v = s_max[idx];
        float norm = (v - mean) * inv_std;
        float o = norm * ln_w[idx] + ln_b[idx];
        o += s_x[idx]; // residual node_i
        out[(b * N + i) * D + idx] = o;
    }
}

torch::Tensor fused_scene_graph_forward(
    torch::Tensor nodes,
    torch::Tensor pair_feats,
    torch::Tensor edge_mask,
    torch::Tensor w1_T,
    torch::Tensor b1,
    torch::Tensor w2_T,
    torch::Tensor b2,
    torch::Tensor ln_w,
    torch::Tensor ln_b)
{
    int B = nodes.size(0);
    int N = nodes.size(1);
    int D = nodes.size(2);
    int P = pair_feats.size(3);
    int H = w1_T.size(1);

    auto out = torch::empty_like(nodes);

    dim3 grid(B, N);
    dim3 block(BLOCK_SIZE);

    int L = 2 * D + P;
    size_t shmem_size = (L + H + D + BLOCK_SIZE) * sizeof(float);

    fused_scene_graph_kernel<<<grid, block, shmem_size>>>(
        nodes.data_ptr<float>(),
        pair_feats.data_ptr<float>(),
        edge_mask.data_ptr<float>(),
        w1_T.data_ptr<float>(),
        b1.data_ptr<float>(),
        w2_T.data_ptr<float>(),
        b2.data_ptr<float>(),
        ln_w.data_ptr<float>(),
        ln_b.data_ptr<float>(),
        out.data_ptr<float>(),
        B, N, D, P, H);

    return out;
}
"""

_fused = load_inline(
    name="fused_scene_graph_v1_opt",
    cpp_sources=cpp_source,
    cuda_sources=cuda_source,
    functions=["fused_scene_graph_forward"],
    extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "--use_fast_math"],
    extra_cflags=["-O3"],
)


class ModelNew(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, dim: int, pair_dim: int, hidden: int):
        super().__init__()
        self.dim = dim
        self.pair_dim = pair_dim
        self.hidden = hidden
        self.fuse = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Linear(2 * dim + pair_dim, hidden),
            nn.SiLU(),
            nn.Linear(hidden, dim),
        )
        self.out_norm = nn.LayerNorm(dim)

    def forward(
        self,
        nodes: torch.Tensor,
        pair_feats: torch.Tensor,
        edge_mask: torch.Tensor,
    ) -> torch.Tensor:
        nodes = nodes.contiguous()
        pair_feats = pair_feats.contiguous()
        edge_mask = edge_mask.contiguous()

        w1_T = self.fuse[0].weight.t().contiguous()
        b1 = self.fuse[0].bias.contiguous()
        w2_T = self.fuse[2].weight.t().contiguous()
        b2 = self.fuse[2].bias.contiguous()
        ln_w = self.out_norm.weight.contiguous()
        ln_b = self.out_norm.bias.contiguous()

        return _fused.fused_scene_graph_forward(
            nodes, pair_feats, edge_mask,
            w1_T, b1, w2_T, b2, ln_w, ln_b
        )
